 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitting a Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Mt. Forest Cemetery was operated by the Mt. Forest Cemetery Association; and
WHEREAS, the Mt. Forest Cemetery Association was dissolved May 22, 1939; and
WHEREAS, Mt. Forest Cemetery is located within unincorporated Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Cook County took responsibility for Mt. Forest Cemetery; and
WHEREAS, Mt. Forest Cemetery has not been maintained for several years; and
WHEREAS, a majority of the gravesites located in Mt. Forest Cemetery have been relocated to Mt.
Glenwood Cemetery; and
WHEREAS, as of 1999 no grave markers were standing and two to three markers have sunk into the
ground; and
WHEREAS, according to 55 ILCS 70/2 the President of the County Board, with the advice and consent
of the County Board may appoint a suitable caretaker for a cemetery; and
WHEREAS, the Village of Thornton is interested in cleaning and maintaining the area known as Mt.
Forest Cemetery; and
WHEREAS, the Village of Thornton is interested in using the property as a nature center, creating a
walkway and posting identification of the trees and foliage on the property.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, Cook County appoints the Village of Thornton as caretaker
of the area known as Mt. Forest Cemetery. As caretaker the Village is allowed to maintain and make
improvements in the area, taking care so as not to disturb any of the gravesites found in the cemetery.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Finance Real Estate Subcommittee (Comm. No. 2368 10) and the Committee
on Roads and Bridges (Comm. No. 236811 ). The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000

ALTERNATE TRAFFIC AND DOMESTIC VIOLENCE COURT SITE
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 19, 2000 from
CARL R. HANSEN and CALVIN R. SUTKER, County Commissioners
In accordance with the Rules of the Board please place the submitted communication on the agenda for
the Cook County Board Of Commissioners for its regularly scheduled meeting of June 20, 2000.
LETTER
June 16, 2000
Honorable Cook County President
John H. Stroger, Jr.
I 18 North Clark Street
Suite 567
Chicago, IL 60602
Re: New Court Facilities/Homan Square
Dear Mr. President,
Submitted please find our proposal for the new Traffic and Domestic Violence Court Facilities, which we
believe, should be built at Homan Square. I would like to address the points below to the County
Commissioners in order to show that these proposals will both qualify the property and justify this project
location.
The proposal, as you will see, is comprised of two prospective plans, to assure the proper fit and function
for the County. The first proposal, "A' ', is for the reconstruction of the existi ng structure and
redevelopment of the property. The second proposal, " B"', covers the construction of new buildings on
the same site.
PLAN "A"
I.

2.

3.

4.

5.

The 3245 West Arthington Building referred to, as the " Allstate Building" is an existing 310,000
square foot facility that can be renovated to meet the requirements for the Traffic Court, and
Mi sdemeanor courtrooms.
The building and the site are bordered on the north Arlington Ave., the west by Homan Ave., the
east by Kedzie Ave., and the South by the railroad embankment. This geography offers both
security, and buffer to any other residents or businesses.
A new 90,000 square foot building would be constructed on the adjoining vacant property to
faci litate the Domestic Violence courtrooms. With the two structures, there will be clear
separation between the two functions of the faci lities, and assist in overall security issues.
There is an existing 1,082 car parking faci lity. This structure lends itself to the addition of
between 2 to 4 additional levels thus facil itating 2,200 parking places. There is a separate 225-car
parking lot at the rear of the building that can be designated fo r Judges, State' s Attorneys, and
clerical staff, again offering additional safety feat ures to these individuals from the general public
utili zing the facilities.
The existing building is connected to the new Homan Square Police Department fo r ease of
prisoner transport, cell housing, and police response to the facilities.

No housing or commercial buildings are effected by this building use, and therefore, there is no
displacement of residents or acquisition of land.
Work on the project can commence immediately, upon plan development and permit issuance
thus not delaying the County' s occupancy during the review process that the County would
undertake.
The property allows for an additional 3. 12 acre vacant area for future expansion of the facilit ies,
or additional adm inistrative or support structures.
The property is located within four short blocks of the rapid transit congress line, and three existing
bus Jines. The 200 I addition of the Homan Square shuttle service will allow train travelers to be
picked up at the Homan station and dropped at the entry door to the Court facilities.
The traffic impact to the area would be less than that which existed while Sears and Roebuck
operated these structures with thirty-five thousand employees.
Access to the fac ilities can be made from Homan Ave., or Kedzie Ave., onto Arthington occupied
only by the same building complex, and without impacting any surrounding homes or business.
The entire project is contained in a campus type setting with gardens, and tree lined walks.
The existing building is connected to an additional 700,000 square feet of professional office
space to faci litate both expansion and the addition of support offices including: The State's
Attorney' s offices, and court support personnel. The adjoining buildings currently faci litate many
governmenta l offices, such as the Attorney General, and General Administration Services, and
many social support agencies such as DCFS, LifeLink, and youth centers.
The infrastructures to the building are new, when the neighborhood was redeveloped.
State of the art communication li nes exist in the adjoi ni ng property already. Satellite placement
on the roof structure is unobstructed by any surrounding buildings.
The faci lity would be set in an Enterprise Zone, Empowerment Zone, and TIF District.
The entire construction and redevelopment project could be completed as a Tenant Build-out.
The County would not have the responsibility of funding the project except for the ir support
requirements such as administration and legal fees. The entire project cost is estimated at
approximately $ 11 2,000,000.00. A lease term for the facilities can be entered for a period of time
as little as 15 years to as Jong as 99 years. The lease pay ments would be offset by the interest
accrued on the savings to the County as shown on the s ubmitted breakdown exhibits.
The entire project can be completed and operating in as little as thirty months.
Change orders due to unforeseen conditions become the responsibility of the Landlord, thus
protecting the County from cost overruns.
Design criteria can be developed which will incorporate construction elements such as the support
columns into the concept design similar to the County Board Room where column distance is
approximately the same or smaller, creating state of the art court rooms at substantial savings.
Visibility of the property can be simply achieved by placement of the Cook County fl ag on the
existing tower, which is c learly visible from the 290 (Eisenhower) expressway, and the possible
incorporation of the County embl em or name on the same structure.
With the placement of the Court facilities at the Homan Square Complex, construction of an
add ition onto the tower, and the redeve lopment of the tower itself would create add itional office
space, Judges private offices and suppor1 facilities, all connected to the court faci lities by
underground walkways.

PLAN "B"
I.

2.
3.
4.

The Landlord will demolish the ex1strng Allstate building, and construct a new facil ity
comprising the entire 400,000 square foot project on the same footprint.
Items 4 through 20 remain the same as in plan "A".
Time frame remains the same.
Cost should remain approximately the same.

Please review the submitted documents. As you will see, we have a llocated generous budgets to
reconstruct the existing building for both appearance and technology. Further we have budgeted
substantial money's for the construction of the new add itional building which would be built on land that
is suited fo r this type of construction without acquisition costs, demolition of existing structures or major
excavation or alteration to the ground.
I am sure that as you look through these documents and have the fi gures reviewed and critiqued, you will
agree that this site is in so many ways suited for this facility, both in substantial savi ngs of money and

W AIYER OF PERMIT FEES
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 25, 2000 from

AGREEMENT RENEWAL
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 26, 2000 from
RUTH M. ROTHSTEIN, Chief, Bureau of Health Services
Re:

Extension of Agreement between Cook County, the Ounce of Prevention and Hektoen
Institute for Medical Research

requesting authorization from the Cook County Board of Commissioners for the Purchasing Agent to
renew the agreement (Contract N umber 98-43- I 284) with the Ounce of Prevention and the Hektoen
Institute for Medical Research regarding the operation of three health centers. The three health centers
are the Bogan/DuSable Health Center located at DuSable High School, the Dawson/ Ford Health Center
located at Beethoven Elementary School and the Hayes Family Health Center located in the Charlie
Hayes Family Investment Center. These three (3) health centers represent a public-private collaboration
between the Cook County Bureau of Health Services, the Ounce of Prevention, the Chicago Public
Schools (CPS), the Chicago Housing Authority (CHA), and the Illinoi s Department of Human Services
(IDHS). This agreement has allowed us to fill a critical health care need for an underserved population;
pre-adolescents, adolescents, young adults and public housing residents.
The Ounce of Prevention and the lllinois Department of Human Servi ces prov ide a grant to support a
portion of the costs of the centers; Cook County provides a portion of the cost through a grant to the
Hektoen Institute; and the CPS and the CHA provide space for the health centers.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $204,630.00. Grant to the Hektoen Institute ($85,262.00 in Fiscal Year 2000;
and $ I I 9,368.00 in Fiscal Year 200 I). Estimated Revenue: $391 ,900.00. ($ I 63,292.00 for Fiscal Year
2000; and $228,608.00 for Fiscal Year 200 I). Agreement period: July I, 2000 through June 30, 200 I.
(893-260 Account).
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Chief of
the Bureau of Health Services be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

OO-R-369
RESOLUTION
STATE OF ILLINOIS
SUPPLEMENTAL RESOLUTION FOR IMPROVEMENT BY COUNTY
UNDER THE ILLINOIS HIGHWAY CODE
BE IT RESOLVED, by the County Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, that the following
described County Highway be improved under the Illinois Highway Code:
County Highway A58, Camp McDonald Road at Tributary A of Mc Donald Creek near Schoenbeck Road;
and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the type of improvement shall be removal and reuse of the existing
two 6 feet 3 inch culverts following installation of timber piles and concrete pile bents and includes,
removal and replacement of bituminous pavement, removal of unsuitable material, backfill, landscaping,
engineering and other necessary highway appurtenances and shall be designated as Section: 99-A58 I 602-BR-MFT; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the improvement shall be constructed by contract; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Three Hundred Thousand
and No/ I 00 Dollars, ($300,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for the
construction of this improvement; and

Office of the Chief Judge to facilitate access to the visitations of children by their non-custodial parents.

I. No exterior lighting allowed.

Your Committee on Finance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Wednesday, June 14, 2000 at the hour of 10:30 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building,
118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois for a public hearing to consider the Proposed New Traffic and
Domestic Violence Court Facility Resolution and Intergovernmental Agreement.
Following the Call of the meeting, Chairman Daley asked the Secretary to the Board to read the meeting
notice into the record.
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
236496

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated June 1, 2000:
PROPOSED NEW TRAFFIC AND DOMESTIC VIOLENCE COURT FACILITY
AND PROPOSED RESOLUTION
On August 4, 1999, thi s honorable body approved a contract with Cook County Court
Associates, a joint venture consisting of Mesirow Stein Real Estate, Inc. and UBM, Inc. to
provide programming and planning services for the proposed New Traffic and Domestic
Violence Court Facility Project ("Phase I"). Phase I has now been concluded.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for Phase II of the New
Traffic and Domestic Violence Court Facility Project. Specific authorization is requested for
the following:

I.

AUTHORIZATION OF THE PROJECT. Phase II consists of the design, site development,
construction, administration, insurance, professional services and the acquisition of land, for a
total budget of $212,340,000.

2.

DESJGNA TION OF THE SITE. The recommended site is bounded by West Jackson
Boulevard on the north, South Spaulding A ven ue on the east, West Congress Boulevard on
the south, and South Homan Boulevard on the west, and is sometimes referred to as " Site I."
It is respectfully recommended that this honorable body designate Site I as the site for the
New Traffic and Domestic Violence Court.

3.

An intergovernmental agreement with the Public Building Commission to acquire the site on
the County ' s behalf. It is further recommended that the Public Building Commission of
Greater Chicago (the " PBC" ) be authorized to carry out the acquisition on behalf of the
County of Cook. Approval of the " RESOLUTION AUTHORIZING THE ACQUISITION
OF PROPERTY BY THE PUBLIC BUILDING COMMISSION OF CHICAGO" is therefore
respectfully requested.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $212,340,000.00. Bond Issue (37000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
NOTE:

This matter was also referred to the Committee on Construction. (See Comm . No. 236495).

The Chairman then asked President Stroger to make a statement regarding the request before the Board.
President Stroger informed the members that today the committee is being asked to consider plans for
development of a modern, 32-room courthouse for a Domestic Violence Court, T raffic Court and
Misdemeanor Courts. The president said that this is the next step towards a comprehensive solution to
the County's court space needs. He continued by saying that if the site is approved, a budget w ill be
established for the project followed by an agreement with the Public Building Commission and the C ity
of Chicago to acquire the land to build the facility.
President Stroger further stated that the Board will work with the residents in the community to establish
fair, just and equitable agreements. He said the Board will reach out to all segments of the community,
including churches, social service organizations, businesses and the young people who have an interest.
The plan is to have a public facility that works for the community to help make the community a better
place for all people in the city and the county.

President Stroger moved approval of the original acreage of 13 acres referred to as "Site 1" and
referenced as Parcels I, II, III, IV, V and VI in Exhibit A of the Resolution (Communication
Number 236496). Seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz.
Commissioner Steele moved to amend the Resolution (Communication Number 236496) to reduce
the original acreage from 13 acres to approximately 8 acres to exclude in Site 1 the line South of
Van Buren Street and thereby removing Parcels IV and V from Exhibit A of the Resolution.
Seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz.

site plan.

Jacqueline Cox, Presiding Judge of the First Municipal District, Patrick McGann, Supervising Judge of
Traffic Court and Robert Bastone, Deputy Pres iding Judge of the First Municipal District.
Chief Judge O ' Connell stated that his office has worked very c losely with President Stroger in planning a
faci lity that will adequately address the needs of the Circuit Court. He said the proposed facility is
flexible in its nature and with changing caseloads, the facility can be utilized as req uired.

President Stroger asked for leave to allow Earl Neal, General Counsel, Public Building Commission to
address the process of compensation for any land acquired for this project.
Mr. Neal stated that the only authority the city, county and Public Building Commission have in tenns of the
amendment offered by Commissioner Steele is that affected property located on the north side of Van Buren
Street to the south side of Jackson from Homan to Spaulding. He said the property south of Van Buren
Street is not affected and cannot be legally acquired, based on the proposal now before the committee.
Mr. Neal went o n to say that the acquisition includes residential, commercial, and vacant parcels. He said
the primary concern is how the fami lies wi ll be treated. He reiterated that the president and every
commissioner has told him that everyone must be treated fairly, must be compensated adequately and
relocation must be provided .
According to Mr. Neal, following is the process by which land acquisition will take place:
1. Notification to property owner that land has been designated fo r use by the county including a
req uest to allow appraisal of property. There will be two appraisals and one must be either a
broker or real estate person from the community.
2.

An offer on the property w ill be made based upon the two appraisals and will be based on the
highest amount determined.

3.

Relocation efforts will be made for property owners. A unique feature of this proposal is that if
the owner purchases a building in Chicago, they will be paid an add itional $5,000.00 above the
val ue of the property at closing.

2085

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
4. Tenants will be paid the actual cost of moving and an additional $ 1,500.00 to assist in obtaining a
new rental unit, security deposit and first month's rent.
A team of brokers will be available to assist in relocation efforts. He concluded by saying that his door
will always be open for anyone wishing to discuss relocation.
Commissioner Hansen asked if any appraisals have been conducted by the Public Building Commission
on the feasibility of locating the courthouse on some of the other sites proposed by the public today,
specifically, sites proposed by Luster Jackson and Reverend Steve Stultz.
Mr. Neal responded that studies have been conducted, but no appraisals have been prepared .
Commissioner Steele asked if low interest loans will be available in the event the appraisal sum is not
adequate to purchase a new home.
Mr. Neal responded that there are a number of subsidized City programs for mortgages or loans. He said
that the project team will make certain all home owners are aware of these programs.
In response to Commissioner Sutker's question regarding re-evaluating the other 8 acre sites, President
Stroger responded that comparison studies have already been completed.
In response to Commissioner Maldonado's question regarding if there were any esti mates on the average
value of the homes in the targeted area, Earl Neal stated that no appraisals were done on individual
homes. However, he explained that based on estimated land values in the area, the total cost of land
acq ui sition is estimated at $6 million.
Commissioner Maldonado stated he hoped the Public Building Commission would consider the New
Homes for Chicago Program for the residents and tenants in the planned site area. The Commissioner said
the program will give the residents great opportunity to purchase a new home with a substantial subsidy.
Commissioner Silvestri stated that the amendment under consideration to reduce the acreage from 13 to 8
acres is a positive change for the community and addresses the majority of the concerns expressed by the
residents in the Homan area south of Van Buren Street.
Commissioner Lechowicz gave background information on this issue. He stated that the Committee on
the Courts for the 2 1•• Century was charged with the responsibility of identifying the future needs of the
Cook County Circuit Court system. He said public hearings were held on August 2, 1999, the present
traffic court location was sold to private developers, the present domestic violence court location is
inadequate and recommendations have been rece ived from the Chief Judge leading to the collaborative
efforts outlined in the report before the committee.
Commissioner Collins stated her concern that the planning process did not have enough community
involvement and suggested that the committee delay taking action on approving the plan in order to
address the community's concerns and impact on the neighborhood .
Commissioner Hansen also stated his concern w ith approving the site plan without further study and
responses from the Project Manager and Public Building Commission.

2086

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
Commissioner Gos lin said he agreed with Commissioners Collins and Hansen and would like to see the
issue deferred for two weeks. He noted the recent zoning issue in Barrington Township where the Board
worked with the residents on a compromise between the township and the community. Commissioner
Goslin stated that he sees a similarity in the Garfield community's concerns of losing their homes.
In response to Commissioner Carr's question regarding if the proposed site would have adequate parking,
courtrooms and landscaping space, the Project Manager responded the building meets the courts' needs
and the space criteria for the project, including 32 courtrooms and 1900 parking spaces.
Commissioner Silvestri asked if there has been any discussion with the City of Chicago regarding the
possible danger of the angled corner at Fifth Avenue?
Mr. Szkatulski responded that there have been preliminary discussions with the Chicago Planning
Department to review the site and make certain that the proposal is not something that would be objected
to at a later date. Discussions have taken place regarding straightening out the angle at the Fifth A venue
intersection to which the City seemed to be receptive.
Chairman Daley asked if all ordinances will be complied with as required by the City a nd the County.
Mr. Szkatulski responded in the affirmati ve.

Commissioner Hansen moved to defer action on the Resolution, as amended (Communication
Number 236496), for two weeks to review other sites and report back to the Finance and
Construction Committees. Seconded by Commissioner Sutker.

OO-R-370
RESOLUTION

RESOLUTION AUTHORIZING THE ACQUISITION OF PROPERTY
BY THE PUBLIC BUILDING COMMISSION OF CHICAGO
ON BEHALF OF THE COUNTY OF COOK
FOR CONSTRUCTION OF A NEW COURTHOUSE
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, Illinois (the "County") is a home rule unit of local government
and a body politic and corporate authorized and empowered to promote the public health, safety and
welfare, furnish essential governmental services through its various departments and agencies and enter
into contractual agreements with units of local government for the purpose of achieving the aforesaid
objectives; and
WHEREAS, the Public Building Commission of Chicago (the "Commission") is a municipal
corporation that was created on March 28, 1956 by ordinance adopted by the City Council (the "City
Council") of the City of Chicago (the "City") pursuant to the Public Building Commission Act, 50 ILCS
20/1 et. seq. (the "Act") for the purpose of facilitating the funding, acquiring and constructing of public
improvements; and
WHEREAS, by resolution adopted on May 8, 1956, the County joined with the City, the Forest
Preserve District of Cook County, the Board of Education of the City of Chicago, the Sanitary District of
Greater Chicago (now known as the Metropolitan Water Reclamation District), and the Chicago Park
District in the organization of the Commission; and
WHEREAS, the Commission has heretofore participated in the acquisition and/or construction of
public buildings, facilities and improvements, including the Chicago Civic Center (now known as the
Richard J. Daley Center) and the Audy Home, on behalf of the County for the conduct of its public
programs and activities; and
WHEREAS, the County has identified a need to construct a facility to house the First Municipal
Traffic Court Division, the Domestic Violence Division and criminal misdemeanor cases previously
heard at 11th and State, to replace facilities which are aging and in need of redevelopment; and
WHEREAS, the County has identified a proposed site for such facility, which site is located in
the City of Chicago, in the block bounded by West Jackson Boulevard on the north, South Spaulding
A venue on the east, West Congress Bot:Jlevara Van Buren Street on the south, and South Homan
Boulevard on the west, and legally described on Exhibit A hereto (the " Subject Property"), for acquisition
and construction of a new courthouse and related and ancillary facilities (the " Project"); and
WHEREAS, the County has confirmed the suitability of the Subject Property through a study by
consultants retained by the County to perform planning and programming services for the Project; and
WHEREAS, it is contemplated that the Project will be comprised of 1) a traffic court and related
facilities, 2) courtrooms and auxiliary functions for the domestic violence cases now located at 13th and
Michigan, and 3) court facilities for criminal misdemeanor cases now located at 11th and Michigan; all on
a site that will be sufficient in size to provide for appropriate architectural settings and adequate
landscaping, parking and ancillary features for such Project; and

2088

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
WHERE AS, in order to facilitate the acquisition of the Subject Property and the construction of
the Project, the County intends to request that the Commiss ion undertake the acquisition of the Subject
Property on behalf of the County for the aforesaid purposes with funds to be provided by the County; and
WH EREAS, the County intends to enter into an intergovernmental agreement (the "Agreement")
with the Commission pursuant to the provisions of Article VII , Section 10 ofthe 1970 Constitution of the
State of Illinois and the Intergovernmental Cooperation Act of the State of Illinois which will set forth the
respective duties and responsibilities of the parties;
NOW, THEREFORE, BE AND IT IS HEREBY RESOLVED by the Board of Commissioners of
the County as follows:
I.

The foregoing recitals are hereby incorporated herein by reference.

It is hereby determined that it is necessary, desirable, and in the best interests of the
2.
citizens of the County, to cause the acquisition of the Subject Property for the purpose of
constructing the Project thereon in order to prov ide consolidated facilities, insofar as practicable,
to be used in the administration and adjud ication of traffic citations, domestic violence and
criminal misdemeanor cases.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 14 of the Act, the County hereby approves the
3.
selection, location and designation of the Subject Property, as legally described on Exhibit A
hereof, for acquisition, improvement, development and construction of the Project.
4.
The Commissio n is hereby requested to undertake the acquisition of the Subject Property
on behalf of the County for the aforesaid purposes, with fund s to be provided by the County
pursuant to the Agreement, and authorized to undertake any and all action which may be
necessary and appropriate in order to effectuate the purposes and objecti ves of this Resolution.
5.
The Pres ident, Comptroller and Secretary of the Board of Commissioners of the County
are hereby authorized, empowered and directed to execute the Agreement between the County
and the Commission, substantially in the form attached hereto and made a part hereof as Exhibit
B, with such modifications as may be authorized by the President, to set forth the procedures and
guidelines to be followed in implementing the acq uisition of the Subject Property.
6.
The County hereby allocates certain amounts not to exceed Ele'"en Million FiYe H1:rndred
Sei,'enty One Thousand five Hundred Dollars ($11,571 ,500.00) Six Million One Hundred FortyEight Thousand Two Hundred Fifty Dollars ($6, 148,250.00) from the proceeds of Bond Account
37000 to pay or reimburse the Commission for costs, expenses and fees incurred in connection
with acquiring the Subject Property, such payment or reimbursement to be in accordance with the
Intergovemmental Agreement.
7.

This Resolution shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage and approval.

, 2000, is made by and

RECITALS
I. The County is a home rule unit of local government and a body politic and corporate that is
authorized and empowered to furni sh essential governmental services including, but not limited to, court
room and related and ancillary facilities for use by the judicial branch of government and other
administrative departments and agencies of the County.
2. The Public Building Comm ission Act of the State of Illinois, 50 TLCS 20/1 , as amended (the
" Act"), provides a means for facilitating the acquisition, construction or enlargement of public
improvements for use by various public agencies in the furnishing of essential governmental, health,
safety and welfare services.
3. On May 8, 1956, the Board of Commissioners of the County joined with the C ity of C hicago
(the "City") and other municipal corporations in the organization of the Commi ssion for purposes of
assisting with the acquisition, development and construction of public improvements, buildings and
faci Iities.
4. The County has identified a need to construct a facility to house the First Municipal Traffic
Court Division, the Domestic Violence Division and criminal misdemeanor cases previously heard at
11th and State, to replace faci lities which are aging and in need of redevelopment.
5. The County has identified and designated a proposed site for such facility, which site is
located in the C ity of Chicago, in the block bounded by West Jackson Boulevard on the north, South
Spaulding Avenue on the east, West CoRgress Bo1:1lei,•ard Van Buren Street on the south, and South
Homan Boulevard on the west, and legally described on Exhibit A hereto (the "Subject Property"), for
acquisition and construction of a new courthouse and related and ancillary facilities (the " Project").
6. The Commi ssion is authorized and empowered by the Act to acquire the fee simple title to
real property, including easements and reversionary interests in streets, alleys and other public places, by
purchase or the exercise of eminent domain, for the construction of public improvements, buildings and
facilities in an area or areas that have been selected, located and approved by the governing bodies of the
County and the Commission.
7. In view of the experience of the Commission in the acquisition and assembly of parcels of
rea l property for the construction of public projects and expertise in the management, supervision and
administration of the land acquisiti on process, the County has determined that it would be cost effective
and efficient for the Comm ission to undertake the acquisition of the Site fo r the Project on behalf of the
County.
8. It is contemplated by the Parties that the costs of acq uiring the Site will be paid by the County
with funds appropriated by the County for the Project and that title to the Site will be conveyed by the
Commission to the County upon completion of land acquisition activities.
9. The Parties have determined that it is in their best interests to enter into this Agreement
pursuant to the Intergovernmental Cooperation Act of the State of Illinois, in order to set forth their
objectives and respective duties and responsibilities and to describe the procedures to be followed for
acquiring title to the various parcels of real estate situated within the Site.
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of the mutual covenants and agreements contained herein,
the Parties hereto hereby agree as follows :

2091

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000

DEFINITIONS
Act: The Public Building Commission Act of the State of lllinois, 1998, 50 ILCS 20/ 1 et. seq., as
amended from time to time.
Authorized Commission Representative: The person or entity employed or retained by the
Commission to administer, coordinate and manage the activities of the Commission and its designees
with respect to the acquisition of the Site.
Authorized County Representative: The person or entity designated by the County as the
person to whom notices shall be given pursuant to this Agreement and otherwise act as the County's
representative in implementing the requirements of this Agreement.
Budget: The budget attached hereto and made a part hereof as Exhibit B as the estimated costs
of acquiring the Site including, without limitation, payments to owners, appraisal fees, title and closing
costs, legal notices and attorneys' fees, surveys, relocation costs and benefits, environmental audits, and
other customary land acquisition fees and expenses.
Commission: The Public Building Commission of Chicago, an Illinois municipal corporation.
County: The County of Cook, a home ru le unit and body corporate and politic of the State of
Illinois.
Project: The development and construction of a new facility to provide replacement court
rooms, ancillary and support facilities and parking for the First Municipal District Traffic Court located at
321 N. LaSalle Street, Domestic Violence Court located at 1340 S. Michigan Avenue and misdemeanor
courts formerly located at 11th and State.
Project Account: An interest-bearing account to be establ ished and maintained by the
Commission for the deposit of funds advanced by the County to pay the costs incurred by the
Commission for acquiring the Site as more fully described in Section 8.2 hereof.
Site: That certain area located in the City of C hicago, County of Cook and State of Illinois,
bounded by West Jackson Boulevard on the north, South Spaulding Avenue on the east, West GoAgress
Boulevard Van Buren Street on the south, and South Homan Boulevard on the west, as legally described
on Exhibit A, to be acquired by the Commission on behalf of the County fo r construction of the Project.

SECTION I
INCORPORATION OF RECITALS
The recitations set forth above constitute an integral part of this Agreement and are hereby
incorporated herein by this reference with the same force and effect as if set forth herein as agreements of
the Parties.

SECTION II
RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE COMMISSION
2.1
The Commission. The Commission hereby agrees to provide all professional and legal
services required to obtain title in and to the Site, free and clear of any encumbrances which could
interfere wi th the use and development of the Site for its intended purpose, and to obtai n all necessary
zoning changes or approvals to permit use and development of the Site for its intended purpose, all in
accordance with the terms and provisions of the Act and this Agreement. Specific responsibilities of the
Commission include the following:

2092

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
2.1.1
Obtain title searches, surveys, appraisal reports, environmental studies and
reports and s uch other assessments and data as may be necessary in order to determine the owner
or owners of and persons interested in and to the parcels of real property to be acquired;
2.1.2 Review and evaluate appraisal reports and other data and factors affecting the
valuation of the parcels of real property to be acquired, and with prior approval of the Authorized
County Representative, prepare written offers for the purchase thereof;
2.1.3 Conduct negotiations with the owner or owners or persons interested in and to
the property to be acquired regarding the purchase of such property, and, with prior approval of
the Authorized County Representative, prepare purchase contracts setting forth the terms and
conditions of purchase;
2.1.4 In the event that voluntary negot1at1ons to acquire such property are not
successful, prepare, file and prosecute complaints for condemnation and other pleadings in order
to acquire property within the Site by the exercise of the power of eminent domain;
2.1.5 Execute all transactions to acquire the property within the Site, whether by deed
or judgment order, including any actions necessary to obtain clear title to any tax delinquent
properties, and file petitions and application in order to obtain the tax exempt status of acquired
property;
2.1.6 Negotiate with the City and any other public or quasi-public agencies or
authorities having ownership or other interests in and to real property situated within the Site in
order to acquire (including acquiring title through vacation of public ways or otherwise, as
necessary or appropriate) fee s imple title, free and clear of any encumbrances which, in the
judgment of the Authorized County Representative, could interfere with the use and development
of the Site for its intended purpose;
2.1.7
In consultation with the authorized representatives of the County, and with the
prior written approval of the Authorized County Representative, establish relocation policies and
guidelines, and implement relocation assistance to persons and businesses displaced as a result of
the construction of the Project, within the limits of the Budget;
2.1.8 Retain such real estate appraisers, consultants, vendors and other finns and
entities as may be necessary in order to assist in the acquisition of the Site and implementation of
land acquisition activities, s ubj ect to prior approval by the Authorized County Representative;
2.1.9 Engage in such interaction, consultation, meetings and other activities with
community organizations, elected officials and other interested parties as may be necessary for
the efficient conduct of land acquisition services;
2.1.10 Diligently pursue acquisition of the Site, making best efforts to complete the
acquisition and necessary zoning actions within twelve months after execution of this Agreement,
and in any event to complete the services to be provided under this Agreement by a date which is
no later than eighteen months after the execution of this Agreement;
2.1.11 Prepare and tile any and all necessary requests and applications for re-zoning,
modifications of zoning ordinances, or modifications of planned development status, negotiate
with the City of Chicago Planning Department, represent the County in hearings with Planning
Committee, Zoning Committee, City Council, and any other bodies or officials pertaining to any
such actions, and perform other services necessary to obtain necessary zoning for the intended
use of the Site; and

2093

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
2.1.12 Provide such additional assistance as shall be agreed by the Parties.
2.2
It is expressly understood and agreed that any and all parcels ofreal estate situated within
the Site that may be acquired by the Commission shall be for the use and benefit of the County and title
thereto shall be conveyed by the Commission to the County upon request as soon as practicable (but in no
event later than 30 days after written request for such conveyance by the Authorized County
Representative) by customary documents of conveyance as approved by the Authorized County
Representative.

SECTION III
RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE COUNTY
3.1
The County. The County shall pay all costs and expenses incurred by the Commission
in connection with the acquisition of real property situated within the Site in such amounts as shall be set
forth in the Budget. It is acknowledged by the Parties that the Budget sets forth a maximum cost which
cannot be exceeded without approval of the Cook County Board of Commissioners. With respect to the
categories of expense within the total Budget, the amount budgeted for any line item may not be exceeded
without prior written approval of the Authorized County Representative and the Authorized Commission
Representative. In no event shall the Commission be obligated to pay any funds which exceed the
amounts provided by the County for land acquisition purposes. Specific responsibilities of the County
include the following:
3.1.1
Designate an authorized representative (the "Authorized County Representative")
to act in the County's behalf for purposes of receiving notices pursuant to this Agreement,
attending meetings, examining documents, rendering timely decisions and other activities
required with respect to the implementation of this Agreement;
3.1.2 Upon request of the Authorized Commission Representative, to provide
infonnation with reasonable promptness to the Commission and its designees regarding the
requirements of the County for the Site and the Project including design constraints and criteria,
scheduling, phasing of construction and other activities with reasonable promptness, to the extent
such information is reasonably necessary for the acquisition of the Site, and if such information is
in the possession of the County or its consultants;
3.1.3 Cooperate with the Commission and its designated representatives in providing
testimony in eminent domain proceedings, executing applications for tax exempt status, rezoning, street and alley vacations and obtaining any other approvals as may be necessary for the
acquisition of the Site or the development of the Project;
3.1.4 Pay all costs incurred by the Commission for land acquisition purposes as
provided in the Budget; and
3.1.5

Provide such additional assistance as shall be agreed by the Parties.

2094

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000

SECTION IV
SITE AVAILABILITY AND ACCESS
4.1
Right of Entry. It is expressly acknowledged and agreed that the County, its employees,
consultants and contractors shall have the right to enter upon any parcels within the Site as may have been
acquired by the Commission for the benefit of the County for purposes associated with developing,
improving and constructing the Project without further authorization by the Commission. The
Commission shall cooperate with the County and its designated representatives in obtaining any and all
approvals pertaining to the use of the Site, and execute any application for building permit, re-zoning or
the like as may be required in order to develop and construct the Project.
4.2
Unpermitted Encumbrances. Neither the Commission nor any of its commissioners,
officials, representatives, designees, agents, successors or assigns shall engage in any financing or other
transaction the effect of which creates an encumbrance or lien upon the Site.

Relocation Assistance. Any person or business that is displaced as a result of the
4.3
acquisition of real property situated within the Site for the construction of the Project shall have the right
to receive relocation assistance based upon the relocation policies and procedures of the Commission, a
copy of which is attached hereto as Exhibit B.
SECTIONV
ENVIRONMENTAL CONDITIONS
5.1
Reports and Studies. The Commission shall provide to the County a copy of any
studies and repo1ts with regard to the environmental condition of the soil of all parcels of real property
within the Site and the geology thereof which may have been obtained by the Commission. The County
or the Commission shall cause to be conducted any additional environmental reports and studies which
are necessary for construction thereon.
Environmental Remediation. In the event that adverse environmental conditions are
5.2
discovered on real property situated within the Site during the acquisition of such parcel, the Commission
will cause the responsible party to undertake the remediation of such adverse environmental condition or,
in the case of parcels that are vacant or the owner or owners thereof are unknown or cannot be located,
the Commission may, with the prior approval of the Authorized County Representative, remediate such
condition with the right to utilize such funds as may be allocated in the Budget for s uch purpose. If,
however, the cost of the environmental remediation action exceeds such contingency funds, the
Commission shall promptly notify the Authori zed County Representative, and the Parties shall mutually
agree upon appropriate action to be taken to fund and complete such remediation.
SECTION VI
ADMINISTRATION OF LAND ACQUISITION
6.1
Notices and Information to the County. The Commission s hall advise the Authorized
County Representative of the status of progress regarding acquisition of the Site on a monthly basis and
upon request provide the County with copies of reports and other documents prepared for the
Commission. As soon as reasonably practicable, the Commission shall provide the Authorized County
Representative with any information which may result in an increase in the Budget or delays in the
schedule.

2095

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
6.2
Participation and Review by the County. The Authorized County Representative shall
have the right to attend meetings with representatives of the Commission and others regarding the Project.
The County will provide to the Commission prompt, accurate and complete information regarding the
requirements of the County for scheduling and phasing of the construction of the Project.

SECTION VII
TITLE INSURANCE
The Commission will order title searches and reports in order to detennine the record owner or owners of
each parcel of real property situated within the Site. Such title reports shall also include easements, liens
and other encumbrances which would preclude the use and development of the Site for its intended
purpose.

SECTION VIII
LAND ACQUISITION COSTS AND FEES
8.1
Cost of Land Acquisition. It is the intent of the Parties that the actual cost of acquiring
title in and to the Site sufficient for completing the construction of the Project (including all constructionrelated activities) shall not exceed the sums specified in the Budget. The fee for the Commission's
services will be included within the Budget and shall not exceed One Dollar ($1.00). If at any time the
Commission determines that the Budget is insufficient to pay the costs of acquisition of the Site, the
Authorized Commission Representative shall immediately notify the Authorized County Representative
in writing, including the amount of the projected shortfall and the reasons for such shortfall, and the
Parties shall agree on any future action as is appropriate.
8.2
Payment of Land Acquisition Costs. The Commission shall prepare and s ubmit to the
Authorized County Representative, on a quarterly basis in advance, the estimated amounts that will be
required to pay land acquisition costs and fees for acquiring the Site during the next succeeding 90 days.
In addition to such quarterly estimates, the Commission shall, upon request therefore, prepare an estimate
of such costs anticipated on an annual basis, for County's budgetary purposes. Requests for payment,
however, shall be made on a monthly basis, for amounts estimated to be required over a 30 day period.
Requests for payment shall be submitted at least 15 days prior to the commencement of the period for
which funding is being requested, and shall be made in such specific form as may be requested by the
County Comptroller. Upon receipt, the Authorized County Representative shall promptly process the
payment request, and present such request for payment by the County Comptroller. In the event that the
amounts requested have not been paid to the Commission within 30 days following the submission of the
payment request, the Commission shall have the right to suspend its performance of this Agreement until
payment is received. The funds received from the County shall be deposited by the Commission into an
interest-bearing account (the " Project Account") established by the Commission to pay eligible land
acquisition costs and fees, in accordance with the Budget. The funds deposited in the Project Account
will be invested by the Commission as directed by the County and interest will accrue for the benefit of
the County.
8.3
Disbursement of Project Costs. The Commission will disburse funds deposited in the
Project Account to pay eligible costs and expenses for acquiring the Site in accordance with the
procedures specified in the separate real estate purchase contracts or judgment orders, as the case may be.
Payments for professional services shall be on the basis of invoices approved by the Commission
pursuant to its usual and customary payment procedures. Copies of such invoices shall be made avai lable
for review upon request by the Authorized County Representative.

2096

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
8.4
Insufficient or Excess Funds. In the event that the amounts deposited by the County
into the Project Account shall be insufficient to complete the acquisition of the Site, the Commission shall
notify the Authorized County Representative in writing and request additional funding. In no event shall
the Commission be obligated to expend any funds for the acquiring the Site in excess of the amounts
provided by the County. Any balance remaining in the Project Account upon completion of the
acquisition of the Site shall be paid by the Commission as directed by the Authori zed County
Representative.

Records; Audit. The Commission shall maintain records and accounts which shall
8.5
include entries of all transactions relating to the expenditure of funds required for the acquisition of the
Site. The County shall have the right to inspect the books and records of the Commission pertaining to
the acquisition of the Site, upon request at all reasonable times. Upon conveyance of title to the Site to
County, the Commission shall deliver to the County all records relating to the expenditure of funds as
well as other records, documentation and files pertaining to the acquisition of the Site and the services
performed pursuant to this Agreement.

SECTIONX
MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS

10.l
E ntire Agreement; Amendment. Except as otherwise provided herein, this Agreement
contains the entire agreement of the Parties with respect to the subject matter herein and supersedes all
prior agreements, negotiations and discussions with respect thereto, and shall not be modified, amended
or changed in any manner whatsoever except by mutual consent of the Parties as reflected by written
instrument executed by the Parties hereto.
10.2
Conflict of Interest. No member of the Board of Commissioners of the Commission nor
any board, department or agency of the County nor any official or employee of the County or the
Commission shall have any financial or ownership interest, direct or indirect, in this Agreement or any
Site; nor shall any such member, official or employee participate in any decision relating to this
Agreement which affects his or her personal interest or the interests of any corporation, partnership or
association in which he or she is directly or indirectly interested. No representative of the County or the
Commission shall be personally liable for the performance of the County or the Commission pursuant to
the terms and conditions of this Agreement.
10.3
Mutual Assistance. The Parties agree to perform their respective obligations, including
the execution and delivery of any documents, instruments and certificates, as may be necessary or
appropriate, consistent with the terms and provisions of this Agreement.
10.4
Disclaimer. No provision of this Agreement, nor any act of the County or the
Commission s hall be deemed or construed by any third persons to create any relationship of third-party
beneficiary, or of principal or agent, or of I imited or general partnership, or of joint venture, or of any
association or relationship involving the County or the Commission.
10.5
Headings. The headings of the various sections and subsections of this Agreement have
been inserted for convenient reference only and shall not in any manner be construed as modifying,
amending or affecting in any way the express terms and provisions hereof.

10.6
Governing Law. This Agreement shall be governed by and construed in accordance
with the laws of the State of Illinois.
10. 7
Successors and Assigns. The terms of this Agreement shall be binding upon the County
and the Commission. None of the rights, duties or obligations under this Agreement may be assigned
without the express written consent of the other Party.

2098

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000

10.8
Severability. If any provision of this Agreement, or any paragraph, sentence, clause,
phrase, or word, or the application thereof, in any circumstance, is held invalid, the remainder of this
Agreement shall be construed as if s uch invalid part were not included herein and the remainder of the
terms of this Agreement sha ll be valid and enforceab le to the fullest extent permitted by law.
10.9
Counterparts. This Agreement shall be executed in several counterparts, each of which
shall constitute an orig inal instrument.

Your Committee has considered the following communications from State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine
with reference to the industrial claims hereinafter mentioned.
Your Committee, therefore, recommends that the County Comptroller and County Treasurer be, and by
the adoption of this report, are authorized and directed to issue checks to the Industrial Commission to be
paid from the Workmen's Compensation Fund.

and as a result she injured her back (acute lumbosacral strain). State's Attorney, Richard A.
Devine, is submitting Industrial Commission Lump Sum Petition and Order No. 98-WC57286 in the amount of $2,555.25 and recommends its payment. (Finance Subcommittee
May 9, 2000). Attorney: John E. Lusak, Law Firm of Lusak and Cobb.

Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Wednesday, June 14, 2000 at the hour of I 0:00 A .M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building,
118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
236492

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 2, 2000:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for Cook County & Courthouse Administration Buildings fire
escape repairs. It is respectfully requested that this honorable body approve this request.
This project provides for repair of four (4) fire escapes at the Cook County Building and three
(3) fire escapes at the Cook County Courthouse Administration Building.
Bond Issue (7000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6-7-00.
236493

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michae l E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 22, 2000:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for Hektoen Building Renovation - Phase I. It is respectfully
requested that this honorable body approve this request.
This project provides primarily for exterior concrete and masonry rehabilitation, painting and
plaza deck coating.
Bond Issue (28000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6-7-00.

2149

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the intended use for the Hektoen Building?
Michael LaMont stated that the laboratories will be moved into the new Cook County Hospital, and the
Administration is currently studying what might be the long-term use of the building.
President Stroger stated the Board of Commissioners. in conjunction with the Bureau of Health, will
ultimately decide the best use for the Hekton Building. President Stroger said there was discussions to
sell the property to Rush Presbyterian Hospital, but the Bureau Chief and her staff decided that they
would continue to use the building as a clinic and office building. Further, the President stated that
whatever decision is made, would begin with the Board of Commissioners.
Commissioner Hansen asked how many square feet are in the Hektoen Building?
Michael LaMont responded that he did not have the figures at this time, but will make them available to
the commissioners after the meeting.
236494

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 22, 2000:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for Medical Equipment, Bid Package #5, miscellaneous storage
shelves and lockers at the New Cook County Hospital. It is respectfully requested that this
honorable body approve this request.
This package consists of shelving, carts, lockers, and storage cabinets located throughout the
hospital.
Bond Issue (22000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6-7-00.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
Commissioner Silvestri asked ifthe fayade rehabilitation at the Cook County Building includes windows?
Michael LaMont stated that the Office of Capital Planning and Policy has not made that deci sion. He
stated that this inspection is being done so that cost estimates can be detennined and recommendations
can be brought before the Board as to what should be done with both the exterior and the windows.
Commissioner Hansen asked ifthe contract states that they will look at the windows?
Michael LaMont responded yes.
Commissioner Hansen asked when will the Commissioners receive a report from R.M. Chin &
Associates?
Michael LaMont stated that R.M. Chin & Associates is completing the inspection and a report should be
received within one month.
Commissioner Hansen asked ifthe consultants will separate the cost for the facade from the windows?
Michael LaMont responded yes.
Commissioner Hansen asked if a specific window has been specified?
Michael LaMont responded that no specific window has been selected. He stated that the consultants
would look at the current windows that are in place.

Commissioner Hansen moved approval of Item Nos. 236492, 236493, 236494 and 236497. Seconded
by Commissioner Silvestri, the motion carried.
Commissioner Hansen moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri. The
motion carried.
Respectfully submitted,

ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 9, 2000 from
JOHN W. DA VIS, Director, Real Estate Management Division
The City of Chicago and the Illinois Medical District have req uested the dedication of certain property
owned by the County of Cook for the purpose of widening South Darnen A venue. Two parcels have been
requested:
1. A 32-foot strip immediate ly west of South Darnen A venue, bordered by West Congress Parkway
on the north and West Harrison Street on the south. This parcel is included in the land which was leased
to The CORE Foundation for the purpose of constructing the CORE Center. The dedication of this
property is contingent on consent by the CORE Foundation and has been submitted to that body for
consideration.
2. A 25.50-foot strip of property located immediately east of South Darnen Avenue, bordered by
West Polk Street on the south and West Ogden A venue on the north. This property is the west 25.50 feet
of a parcel whic h was vacated by the C ity of C hicago in 1997 for the benefit of the County, to provide
add iti onal property for the construction of the Hospital. The parcel which is now being dedicated wi ll not
affect the completed Hospital structure.
Michael LaMont, Director of the Office of Capita l Planning and Policy, has informed this office that he
and Walsh/Riteway Joint Venture have met extensively with the City and the Illinois Medical District to
coordinate th is work in order that the road widening does not interfere with the construction of the New
Cook County Hospita l. The City has agreed to delay work on the property to be dedicated unti l
November 1, 2000. By that time, the construction trai lers now on the property can be removed. Further,
the City has agreed to re locate the construction fence placed on the property by the County's contractor
prior to beginning its construction.

2 155

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
Based upon the foregoing, approval of the Ordinance for Dedication and Plats of Dedication is hereby
recommended. The Cook County State's Attorney has reviewed the Ordinance for Dedication and will
approve as to form upon consent by the CORE Foundation and acceptance by the City of Chicago.

00-0-20
ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago vacated a portion of South Darnen Aven ue, pursuant to an
ord inance passed by the City Counci l of Ch icago at a regular meeting held on June 4, 1997 (Document
#97-1435) and said ordinance was fil ed with the Cook County Recorder of Deeds on June 27, 1997 as
Document #97-46729 1; and
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago now desires that a part of the previously vacated South Darnen
A ven ue, located adjacent to the new Cook County Hospital, be rededicated by the County of Cook to the
City of C hicago for purposes of widening Darnen A venue, specifically the rededication of 25.50 feet for
additional right of way on the east side of South Darnen A venue, lying between the southeasterly line of
W. Ogden Avenue and the north line of W. Polk Street, as shown and legally described on the Plat of
Rededication, a copy of which is attached hereto as Exhibit A ("Parcel l "); and
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago also desires that another portion of Darnen A venue, located
adjacent to the CORE Center, be dedicated by the County of Cook to the City of Chicago for purposes of
widening Darnen A venue, specifically 32.00 feet for additional right of way on the west s ide of South
Darnen Avenue, lying between the south line of W. Congress Parkway and the north line of W. Harrison
Street, as shown and legally described on the Plat of Dedication, a copy of which is attached hereto as
Exhibit B ("Parcel 2"); and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners, after due investigation and
consideration, has determined that the public interest shall be served by the dedication of a part of its
property to allow the widening of South Darnen A venue, described in the following ordinance.
NOW THEREFORE, BE IT ORDA INED BY THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF
COMMISSIONERS :
SECTION I. The followi ng described property is hereby rededicated, subject to the terms
conta ined herein, by the COUNTY OF COOK, grantor, to the CITY OF C HI CAGO, grantee, as the
public interest wi ll be served by such rededication:
Parcel I:
The West 25.50 feet of that part of vacated South Darnen A venue in the West 1/2 of the Southeast
I /4 of Section 18, Township 39 North, Range 14 East of the Third Principal Meridian per
Document No. 097- 1435 (recorded as Document #97-467291 ), bounded and described as follows :
Beginning at the point of intersection of the North line of West Polk Street (66 feet in w idth) with
the east line of South Darnen Avenue (11 9.25 feet in width); thence North 89 degrees 52' 30" East
along the North li ne of said West Polk Street, a distance of 25.50 feet; thence North 00 degrees
IO' IO" West a long a line 25.50 feet East of and parallel with the East line of South Darnen Avenue
aforesaid, a distance of 458.46 feet to a point in the Southeasterly line of West Ogden Avenue (80
feet in w idth); thence South 42 degrees 38'00" West along the Southeasterly line of said West
Ogden Avenue, a distance of 37.53 feet to its intersection with the East line of South Darnen
Avenue aforesaid; thence South 00 degrees IO' IO" East along the East line of said South Darnen
Avenue, a distance of 430.90 feet to the point of beginning, all in Chicago, Cook County, Il linois as
striped and indicated by the words " HEREBY REDEDICATED" on the Plat of Rededication, a
copy of which is attached hereto as Exhi bit A, which plat for greater certainty, is hereby made a
part of th is ordinance.

2 156

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
This rededication is made with the express understanding that the CITY OF CHICAGO accepts such
rededication subject to any defect in or lien or encumbrance on the title or unmarketability of title.
Accordingly, this rededication is subject to any and all encumbrances, including easements, covenants,
conditions and restrictions either of record or now existing.
The President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners shall signify the making of said rededication
by the County of Cook by executing the certification of rededication contained on the Plat of
Rededication, a copy of which is attached hereto as Exhibit A.
SECTION 2. The City of Chicago hereby agrees to accept and maintain the existing 12-inch
sewers and appurtenances in the property to be rededicated and such sewers and appurtenances will be
public sewers maintained by the City of Chicago. If and when the existing l 2-inch sewers and
appurtenances are abandoned, the City of Chicago is responsible for the abandonment plans.
SECTION 3: This rededication is subject to the grant of easement contained in the City of
Chicago' s ordinance of vacation, filed with the Cook County Recorder of Deeds as Document #97467291 , whereby an easement was given by the City of Chicago for the benefit of Commonwealth Edison
Company and Ameritech Illinois, their successors or assigns, to operate, maintain, construct, replace, and
renew overhead poles, wi res, and associated equipment and underground conduit, cables, and associated
equipment for the transmission and distribution of electrical energy and telephonic and associated
services under, over, and along S. Darnen Avenue as herein vacated, with the right of ingress and egress.
SECTION 4. The rededication herein provided is made upon the express condition that the CITY
OF CHICAGO shall relocate the temporary fence installed by the County's contractor in connection with
the County 's new Cook County Hospital project prior to commencing work on Parcel I. The County or
its contractor s hall not be responsible for relocating such fence.
The rededication of County property contained herein will require the general contractor for the new
Cook County Hospital (located along Darnen A venue between Polk and Ogden Avenues) to relocate its
staging areas, office trailers and utility hook-ups for construction. In order to minimize any cost to the
County or its general contractor for such relocation, the CITY OF CHICAGO has agreed to schedule its
work on Parcel I to commence after November I, 2000. The rededication of Parcel I is made in reliance
on this schedule. If the schedule is modified and by reason of such modification any costs are incurred by
the County or its General Contractor due to the rededication of Parcel 1, such cost shall be paid by the
CITY OF CHICAGO. Furthermore, as a result of the rededication of the parcel, general contractor states
that access to the construction site may become a challenge and may therefore require the general
contractor to change construction means and methods. Any increased costs due to such necessary
construction means and methods shall be paid by the CITY OF CHICAGO.
SECTION 5. The rededication herein provided for is made upon the express condition that
within 120 days after the passage of this ordinance, the CITY OF CHICAGO shall signify herein its
acceptance of this rededication, subject to the terms contained herein, and shall file or cause to be filed for
record in the Office of the Recorder of Deeds of Cook County, Illinois, a certified copy of this ordinance,
together with the Plat of Rededication, a copy of which is attached hereto as Exhibit A where the CITY
OF CHICAGO shall secure prior to recording: the approval of the Superintendent of Maps; and a
statement contained on the Plat of Rededication by the Chicago Department of Revenue that there are no
unpaid assessments due against the property and a statement by the County Clerk that there are no unpaid
taxes or special assessments against the property.

2157

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
SECTION 6. The following described property is hereby dedicated, subject to the terms
contained herein, by the COUNTY OF COOK, grantor, to the CITY OF CHICAGO, grantee, as the
public interest will be served by such dedication:
Parcel 2:
The East 32.00 feet of Block 2 in McGrath's Addition to Chicago in the East 1/2 of the Northwest
I /4 of Section 18, Township 39 North, Range 14 East, of the Third Principal Meridian, in Cook
County, Illinois as striped and indicated by the words "HEREBY DEDICATED" on the Plat of
Dedication, a copy of which is attached hereto as Exhibit B, which plat for greater certainty, is
hereby made a part of this ordinance.
This dedication is made with the express understanding that the CITY OF CHICAGO accepts such
dedication subject to any defect in or lien or encumbrance on the title or unmarketability of title.
Accordingly, this dedication is subject to any and all encumbrances, including easements, covenants,
conditions and restrictions either of record or now existing.
The President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners shall signify the making of said dedication by
executing the certification of dedication contained on the Plat of Dedication, a copy of which is attached
hereto as Exhibit B.
SECTION 7. Parcel 2 is a portion of a larger parcel of land that has been leased to the CORE
Foundation, an Illinois not-for-profit corporation, under a long-term lease, dated 1/23/97 by and between
the County of Cook as Ground Lessor and the CORE Foundation as Ground Lessee (the "Ground
Lease"). The CORE Foundation subsequently leased this land back to the County of Cook under a longterm building and land lease ("Building and Land Lease"). The CORE Foundation's consent to the
rededication of Parcel 2 and its exclusion from the Ground Lease and Building and Land Lease must be

The COUNTY OF COOK ' S execution of this dedication and the CORE Foundation ' s consent to the
dedication of Parcel 2 may be executed in counterparts, each of which shall constitute an original, but all
of which, when taken together, shall constitute but one agreement. All executed counterparts shall be
returned to John W. Davis, Director of Real Estate Management for the COUNTY OF COOK, 69 West
Washington, Suite 1060, Chicago, Illinois 60602; 312/603-0040. Upon receipt, Real Estate Management
will assemble the counterparts into an original and have the dedication presented to the CITY OF
CH ICAGO for acceptance.
SECTION 8. The rededication herein provided for is made upon the express condition that
within 120 days after the passage of this ordinance, the CITY OF CHICAGO shall signify herein its
acceptance of this dedication, subject to the tenns contained herein, and shall file or cause to be filed for
record in the Office of the Recorder of Deeds of Cook County, Illinois, a certified copy of this ordinance,
together with the Plat of Dedication, a copy of which is attached hereto as Exhibit B, where the CITY OF
CHICAGO shall secure prior to recording: the approval of the Superintendent of Maps; and the Plat of
Dedication shall contain a statement by the Chicago Department of Revenue that there are no unpaid
assessments due against the property and a statement by the County Clerk that there are no unpaid taxes
or special assessments against the property.

OO-R-372
RESOLUTION

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,

MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Mount Carmel is a Catholic, college preparatory high school for boys located in the
Woodlawn community of Chicago just west of Jackson Park and south of the University of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, at the invitation of Chicago Archbishop Patrick E. Feehan, the Carmel ites established the
school then known as St. Cyril College in the fall of 1900; and
WHEREAS, from its early days of less than two hundred students, Mount Carmel has grown to see years
when the student body numbered over one thousand young men; and
WH EREAS, during the turbulent era of the sixties, when many urban Catholic high schools closed their
doors or relocated their campuses, Mount Carmel remained committed to the Woodlawn community and
instituted aggressive programs of transportation and fu nd raising to remai n a vital institution; and
WHEREAS, today the student body numbers approximately 830 students from numerous neighborhoods
withi n Chicago as well as from over forty s uburban communities in Illinois and Northwest Indiana; and
WHEREAS, throughout its history Mount Carmel has forged a reputation for academ ic excel lence.
Consistently, more than ninety-five percent of its graduates go on to success at the college level; and
WHEREAS, in 1984 Mount Carmel was the first Catholic high school in Chicago to be designated as an
"Exemplary School" by the United States Department of Education; and
WHEREAS, Mount Carmel's reputation in athletics is supported by the record books: eight state
championships and nine City Prep Bowl championships in football; five state championships and twenty
Kennedy Cup (Catholic League) championships in hockey; and three consecutive state championships in
wrestling. Mount Carmel also has won a state championship in water polo and was the first Catholic high
school in history to win a state championship in Class AA boys basketball. In recent years its reputation
has expanded as the baseball team won six out of seven Catholic League championships; and
WHEREAS, as it begins its second centu ry, Mount Carmel remains fi rmly planted in the same Woodlawn
communi ty it has served for one hundred years; and

2 160

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000
WH ER EAS, after one hundred years, the Carmelite commitment to educating young men of character
through outstanding spiritual, academ ic and extracurricular programs is as vital as ever. Having made its
contribution to the history of C hicago throughout the twentieth century, Mount Carmel begins the new
millennium with zeal and enthusiasm for maintaining its reputation as one of Chicago's outstanding high
schools; and
WHEREAS, th is Body takes great pride in recognizing those ed ucational institutions which are noted for
their achievements and contributions.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Mount Carmel High School and its principal, Father Carl Markelz, teachers, and staff
for their long-standing service to the comm unity and extend its best wishes for a joyous Centennial
Celebration on Saturday, July 15, 2000 at the Navy Pier Grand Ball Room, Chicago, 1llinois; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that th is text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and an official copy of same be presented to Mount Carmel High School, and to Father Carl
Markelz, Principal , to commemorate this historic milestone.
Approved and adopted this 20th day of June 2000.
JOHN H . STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commi ssioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Calling upon the President and the Cook County Board of Commissioners to create a
task force to study the disparity in the juvenile justice system's treatment of non-minority
and minority youth, and to make recommendations based on its objective findings.

2162

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000

WHEREAS, in recent weeks there have been several articles in the newspapers [Apri l 25, 2000,
" Minority Youth Jailed More'', April 26, 2000, "National Study Concludes Bias Infects the Juvenile
Justice System", May 5, 2000, " The Color of Justice" (Chicago Tribune), and May 19, 2000, " Minority
teens more often tried as adults" (Chicago Sun-Times)] addressing the problems highlighted by a national
study concluding bias in the juvenile justice system nat ionwide, and
WHEREAS, all charging decisions on juvenile cases rest solely with the local police departments, and
WHEREAS, the States Attorney 's office can only provide legal advice when contacted by the police
departments investigating crimes alleged to have been committed by juveniles other than homicides, and
WHEREAS, the employment of station adjustments in the case of minority juveniles is not an option
regularly used, and
WHEREAS, the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987 automatically transfers juveniles 15 and 16 years of
age to adult court if charged with selling drugs within I 000 feet of a school or public housing
development, and
WHEREAS, of the 363 juvenile drug cases transferred to Cook County Criminal Court from 1995
through 1999, 99% of the youth charged as adults were minorities, and
WHEREAS, the criteria for a judicial waiver of juveniles to adult court must be looked at and analyzed
to insure fair and equitable application [racia l breakdown of waiver rate], and
WHEREAS, a racial breakdown of sentencing and case disposition of juveniles processed in Juveni le
and C riminal court is needed to determine the harshness and severity of sentences given.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED THAT, the President and the Members of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners create a task force to study any disparities apparent in the j uvenile justice system
and bring back to thi s Board suggestions based on its obj ective findings to correct prob lems, and to insure
equal protection for all juveniles.
Approved and adopted this 20th day of June 2000.
JOHN H. STROG ER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County C lerk

Com missioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
