GAY AND LESBIAN PRIDE MONTH
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is made up of a diverse population with representation of virtually
every major ethnic and minority group in the world; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is proud of our distinct record of accomplishment in terms of providing
equality, access and opportunity to all our citizens; and
WHEREAS, a sizeable minority of Cook County residents identify themselves as Gay and Lesbian
citizens; and
WHEREAS, Gay and Lesbian citi zens of Cook County, and the United States generally, have made
significant contributions to society in the arts, sciences, fields of research and recreation, business,
entertainment and public service; and
WHEREAS, thi s Honorable Body, in 1999, in an act which brought it in line with thousands of other
large employers and hundreds of other governments across the United States, granted domestic
partnership benefits to our Gay and Lesbian employees; and
WHEREAS, the month of June has by recent tradition been set aside by citizen groups and governments
across the United States as Gay and Lesbian Pride Month; and
WHEREAS, Mayor Richard M. Daley and the City of Chicago have set aside the month of June as Gay
Pride Month and the day of June 25th for the city to host the Gay and Lesbian Pride Day Parade; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook wishes to express the same type of support and spirit of community;
now
THEREFOR E BE IT RESOLVED that the Cook County Board of Commiss ioners does hereby declare
the month of June of the year 2000 as Gay and Lesbian Pride Month in Cook County, Illinois and that we
offer our support and congratulations to the Gay and Lesbian Community for the recent gains they have
made in their purs uit of social equality; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the officia l proceedings of this Honorable
Body.

WHEREAS, in June 2000, the Village of Riverside will celebrate its I25th Anniversary and its 131 st
year of existence; and

designed and created under Olmsted's Plan of 1869; and
WHEREAS, in 1972, the United States Department of the Interior designated the Village of Riverside as
a National Historic Landmark which is the highest designation that can be given by the United States to
an historic site; and
WHEREAS, much of Olmsted's original plan of 1869 remains intact and the Village of Riverside works
diligently to preserve and maintain this plan; and
WHEREAS, the Village is home to approximately 9,200 residents who live, work, shop, play, go to
church and go to school in a community which is universally acknowledged as one of the most beautiful
communities in the world; and

2168

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 20, 2000

from around the world to see first hand the genius of Olmsted.

Board of Commissioners extends to the residents of the Village of Riverside its warmest congratulations
on the occasion of its anniversaries and tenders its gratitude to the residents of the Village of Riverside
who recognize its historical importance and their role in acting as stewards of this beautiful and
significant site; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the text of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of this Honorable Body, and that a suitable copy be provided to the Village of Riverside as evidence of
the admiration in which the Members of this Body hold this community.

THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the President and the Members of the Board of Commissioners
of Cook County take this opportunity on behalf of the staff, residents and patients of Oak Forest Hospital
of Cook County to express gratitude and appreciation to the Franciscan Friars for their outstanding
ministry, and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and a copy thereof be transmitted as a testimonial of the high esteem and appreciation in which the
Franciscan Friars are regarded by the Members of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County.

Approved and adopted this 20th day of June 2000.

JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
